- **From:** Wayne Brown <fwbrown@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 2004-03-10T12:51:49+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.software.year-2000,comp.programming,comp.lang.cobol,news.groups
- **Message-ID:** `<FbE3c.6472$p77.2952@bignews3.bellsouth.net>`
- **References:** `<c1lfc3$1k5bdq$1@ID-193590.news.uni-berlin.de> <403e5308@news2.power.net.uk> <403F8296.37FC1FCB@mb.sympatico.ca> <mmeo40lk2jrgpsdgusdtmnlo1pc65fbl95@4ax.com> <gYY2c.361$qP2.1181@news.indigo.ie> <104q0g02pejua35@corp.supernews.com> <nvgq405vad48qqm0ptf05igp3a4qh1mk20@4ax.com> <104sr69m54dknf1@corp.supernews.com>`

```
In news.groups LX-i <lxi0007@netscape.net> wrote:
> 
> Speaking of artifactual machines - I got rid of my Commodore 64s a 
> couple of years ago.  The Mrs. didn't like them hanging out in the 
> garage any more.  Did they make a COBOL for the C-64?  All I ever used 
> was BASIC.

Yes, "Nevada COBOL" and "Nevada Fortran" were available for the C64.
Both required the CP/M package (which consisted of a Z80 coprocessor
cartridge and CP/M boot diskettes). The COBOL was a bit crippled -- e.g.,
no nested IF statements allowed -- but it was suitable for learning.
In fact, it helped me get my first programming job; I was a mainframe
operator at the time, and my boss was impressed that I had learned COBOL
on my own time just because I was interested.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Discussion: rmgroup comp.software.year-2000

_(thread depth: 10)_

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-03-10T16:24:19-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0403101624.386be828@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<c1lfc3$1k5bdq$1@ID-193590.news.uni-berlin.de> <403e5308@news2.power.net.uk> <403F8296.37FC1FCB@mb.sympatico.ca> <mmeo40lk2jrgpsdgusdtmnlo1pc65fbl95@4ax.com> <gYY2c.361$qP2.1181@news.indigo.ie> <104q0g02pejua35@corp.supernews.com> <nvgq405vad48qqm0ptf05igp3a4qh1mk20@4ax.com> <104sr69m54dknf1@corp.supernews.com> <FbE3c.6472$p77.2952@bignews3.bellsouth.net> <oiE3c.16217$6y1.974564@news20.bellglobal.com>`

```
Donald Tees <donald_tees@nospam.sympatico.ca> wrote

> MicroFocus, Nevada, and MicroSoft all had Cobol's that would run under 
> DOS. MicroFocus was by far the first, having a compiler that ran under 
> CPM-86 and MPM-86 well before the PC.

I think that you meant CP/M-80.

Actually I think that Microsoft's may have been the first to run under
DOS.  Their PC-DOS version of their CP/M-80 Cobol was availble very
early with PC-DOS.

MicroFocus CIS Cobol for CP/M-80 was 1978 or so and appears to have
derived from the founder's previous work for ICL Dataskill in
producing ICL 1500 Cobol around 1977, perhaps earlier the 2nd edition
was 1977.

MicroSoft's Cobol for CP/M-80 was 1979.  There were also versions for
other Z80 machines such as the touchpad POS terminal (as used by Pizza
Hut in UK in the 80s).

RM Cobol also had a CP/M-80 and MP/M version as well as Oasys 8bit
around 1979.
```

```
Richard wrote:
> Donald Tees <donald_tees@nospam.sympatico.ca> wrote
> 
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
> around 1979.

I was thinking of the Altos, actually. It ran MP/M-86 on six terminals, 
and was 8088 based. The latter ones were 8086. Quite a nice OS, 
actually. Completely time-sliced timesharing(no security to speak of), 
and a bit weak in the ability to prioritize, but nicer than anything up 
until cheap networks. As I remember CP/M-86, it morphed into MP/M-86 
almost imediately.  CP/M-80 was 3-4 years earlier than that. I was using 
PDP-11 & 8's during the first couple of years of the s-100 bus. Did'nt 
really get involved with the z-80 stuff and CP/M-80.

I'm pretty sure it was a MicroFocus compiler, but a bit hazy on the 
year. Several years before the PC, for sure, and I would think close to 
the mid seventies.

Donald
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Discussion: rmgroup comp.software.year-2000

_(thread depth: 12)_

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-03-10T23:19:16-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0403102319.7ef3128@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<c1lfc3$1k5bdq$1@ID-193590.news.uni-berlin.de> <403F8296.37FC1FCB@mb.sympatico.ca> <mmeo40lk2jrgpsdgusdtmnlo1pc65fbl95@4ax.com> <gYY2c.361$qP2.1181@news.indigo.ie> <104q0g02pejua35@corp.supernews.com> <nvgq405vad48qqm0ptf05igp3a4qh1mk20@4ax.com> <104sr69m54dknf1@corp.supernews.com> <FbE3c.6472$p77.2952@bignews3.bellsouth.net> <oiE3c.16217$6y1.974564@news20.bellglobal.com> <217e491a.0403101624.386be828@posting.google.com> <404FC20A.70003@nospam.sympatico.ca>`

```
Donald Tees <donald_tees@nospam.sympatico.ca> wrote 

> I was thinking of the Altos, actually. It ran MP/M-86 on six terminals, 
> and was 8088 based. The latter ones were 8086. Quite a nice OS, 
> actually. 

I did use MP/M II on 8 bit and went straight to Concurrent-CP/M-86 3.x
which was rather better than MP/M-86 as it had concurrent virtual
terminals - ie multi-tasking at each terminal.

> Completely time-sliced timesharing(no security to speak of),

There was password protection on directories and files built into the
OS.
 
> and a bit weak in the ability to prioritize, 

256 levels of priority, I did have programs that changed the priority,
but usually a MP/M or CCP/M system running an accounting type system
had spare CPU time because the queue was at the hard disk.

> but nicer than anything up until cheap networks. 

Often a multiuser system would outperform a network using Cobol
accounting systems because the disk access was done directly on the
machine where the program was running.  With a network each station
was saturating the network by dragging the index blocks from the
server on every record read.

> As I remember CP/M-86, it morphed into MP/M-86 almost imediately.  

MP/M-86 derived from MP/M II, not from CP/M-86. The CP/M and MP/M
lines didn't have much code in common beyond the ability to run the
CP/M programs.

> I'm pretty sure it was a MicroFocus compiler, but a bit hazy on the 
> year. Several years before the PC, for sure, and I would think close to 
> the mid seventies.

I don't think so.  Microfocus CIS Cobol for 8 bit was 1978, but
MP/M-86 did not get released until October 1981 according to my
references, which was marginally after the IBM-PC of September 1981.

CP/M-86 was first released in Jan 1981 so even that was only
marginally ahead of the IBM-PC and PC-DOS.

I still use the latest derivitive of Concurrent-CP/M-86 - IMS Real/32.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Discussion: rmgroup comp.software.year-2000

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-02T09:11:55-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c22f8r$jl7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<c1lfc3$1k5bdq$1@ID-193590.news.uni-berlin.de> <c1sqg1$48o$1@panix2.panix.com> <d31d3207.0403012346.476e7eb@posting.google.com>`

```

"Jbaloun" <yonatan62@yahoo.com> wrote in message
news:d31d3207.0403012346.476e7eb@posting.google.com...
> ... The coding job of all time, and nobody noticed.
>  ... Any clued yet as to what actually happened in 2000? No? I thought so.

Actually, I have heard of two fairly significant things that happened from
reliable sources, though neither actually occurred in 2000.

One European bank discovered in I think '97 that their application software
was riddled with Y2K problems that *would* impact them, and that the cost of
revising their existing software to prevent these problems would eat up
their profits for several years.  They voluntarily merged with a larger
bank, scrapped their own software entirely, and were incorporated into the
larger bank's existing application software (which was already "Y2K ready").

One Asian automobile manufacturer discoverd somewhere around '98 that
brand-new long-shelf-life parts were being shipped back because their
expiration dates had a two-digit year past 1/1/2000; the highly-automated
warehouse processes were rejecting the parts as expired and selecting them
for return.  Some parts actually made several trips across the Pacific, at
considerable cost to the company, before this glitch was noticed and
corrected.

    -Chuck Stevens
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Discussion: rmgroup comp.software.year-2000

- **From:** Joe Bernstein <joe@sfbooks.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-08T02:28:45+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.software.year-2000,comp.programming,comp.lang.cobol,news.groups
- **Message-ID:** `<c2glot$mr$1@reader2.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<c1lfc3$1k5bdq$1@ID-193590.news.uni-berlin.de> <c1sqg1$48o$1@panix2.panix.com> <d31d3207.0403012346.476e7eb@posting.google.com>`

```
Followups redirected to what I suspect is the right group; it's not a 
group I read, so if you follow up to this post and don't send me a copy,
don't expect me to see it.

In article <d31d3207.0403012346.476e7eb@posting.google.com>,
Jbaloun <yonatan62@yahoo.com> wrote:

> Double digits are here to stay and the world goes on it's merry way.
> Besides if the programmers can rewrite all the code ever written in a
> few years, they can fix anything. Lights stayed on. Every line of code
> in its proper place. The coding job of all time, and nobody noticed.

Um, speak for yourself.

I worked as an accounting clerk, 1998-2002, and every job that lasted
more than a couple of weeks, up to at least early 2001, was driven in
one way or another by Y2K-related computer system conversions.  Even
when the actual Y2K problems themselves were fixed, the companies 
involved were either working to take advantage of the added features
of their new programs, or upgrading other systems that hadn't been
vulnerable to Y2K but had been identified, in the Y2K planning, as
outdated.

So *I*, anyway, noticed plenty.

And many thanks, you guys, for the most sustained employment I had in
my career as a temp.

Joe Bernstein
```

```
>     This is a discussion concerning the removal (rmgrouping)
>of the newsgroup "comp.software.year-2000".  This is not a
>formal call for votes, nor is it a threat of rmgrouping the
>newsgroup without a vote.


A woman [Jamie] approached the Pearly Gates, and Saint Peter asked for
her social security number.  The woman told him, and Saint Peter typed
on his workstation: pearly-gates:~/peter grep 212-53-6432
/earth/human/status

The computer responded:
212-53-6432 Jamie Andrews ja@dragon.com!earth
<mailto:cms@dragon.com!earth>
naughty pearly-gates:~/peter

Saint Peter then told her she was eternally damned, and that a minivan
to hell would be arriving shortly. Jamie began to protest "but what
did I do wrong?  I loved my fellow neighbor as I loved myself, I was a
kind, warm, gentle person!  Surely there must be a mistake!"

So, Saint Peter looked up on the files, and saw, lo and behold that
she truly was a kind, warm, gentle person...until he saw the entry for
Jan 7, 1992-earth, which read:

***DAMNABLE VIOLATION #69*** Posted irrelevant article to newsgroup.
After probing a little more, Saint Peter explained to the woman "It
seems that on January 7, 1992 you posted an article to
Alt.religion.computers. This article gave no praise of Emacs, no snide
remarks toward Microsoft, and not even a comment on the proper
definition of 'hacker'!  In fact, the article was not even relating to
computers at all, and discussed, of all things, human religion!  There
wasn't even a reference to Bob or Discordianism, Zen, or the Tao of
programming.  Oh dear, this is terrible."

"You see, heaven is a perfect place, and we only have room for the
most perfect people.  Ever since we ran the T-3 line up from New
Jersey we've been particularly harsh on breakers of netettiquite. 

Didn't you read RFC-23654?  The one proposing commandments 11 through
15?" He opened up an XTerm window and searched for some files.  After
a few moments, the laser printer spat out a crisp sheet of paper.  It
read:

11: Thou shalt not flame spelling or grammar.

12: Thou shalt not have a .sig file longer than 3 lines.  13: Thou
shalt not send "All PC Users must die" messages to 19 random groups.

14: Thou shalt not request post a frequently asked question.

15: Thou shalt not post to a group without first reading a week's
worth of posts, thereby avoiding irrelevant articles.

16: Thou shall not post administrative requests to the main list.

When she was done, she began to stammer, but Saint Peter stopped her,
saying "I'm sorry.  There's nothing I can do.  To register a
complaint, you'll have to send mail to
status-change-request@godvax.heaven.com
<mailto:status-change-request@godvax.heaven.com> .

 We have a group of cherubim who manage such requests.  But be sure
you don't send it to status-change@godvax.heaven.com
<mailto:status-change-request@godvax.heaven.com> ,  otherwise your
request will be distributed to the whole mailing list.  They *hate*
that!  In fact, there's some discussion about making that the 16th
commandment..." 

At that point, a Dodge minivan drove up and came to a stop.  Satan, in
the form of an IBM salesperson, stepped out.  "Welcome!", she said.
"We've been waiting for you..."  Jamie, almost in a trance, stepped
into the minivan and was whisked away to the netherworld, a world of
COBOL, System 36's, punch cards, incompatible network standards, and
irresponsible news posters.

Satan turned to Jamoe, and smiled.  "You'll like it here", she said,
"We have netnews, but we've greatly simplified it.  We have only one
group, it's alt.talk.sci.comp.soc.rec.misc!"
===========================================================
```

## Thread: Fujitsu PowerCobol — 3 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### Fujitsu PowerCobol

- **From:** "Euromercante" <euro@dsdd.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-01T13:56:22
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4043673d$0$28136$a729d347@news.telepac.pt>`

```
Hi,
    I've made an exe file (PCExample.exe) in PowerCobol with 3 forms
(PCform1, PCform2, PCform3) and the starting form is PCform2.
    What I would like to ask if it's possible in the command line to call
the exe file referecing the form to open, this is :
        - c:\PowerCobol\PCExample.exe -> this will open the PCform2,
and what I would like to do this:
        - INVOKE POW-SELF "CALLForm" USING "PCform3" "PCExample.exe"
in the command line. It's possible??

Thanks
```

#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu PowerCobol

- **From:** "JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-01T18:40:15-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<M5ydnR1VbfB5St7dRVn-uA@giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<4043673d$0$28136$a729d347@news.telepac.pt>`

```
Euromercante wrote:
> Hi,
>     I've made an exe file (PCExample.exe) in PowerCobol with 3 forms
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> Thanks

No.

One solution is another form, PCform0, as the starting form that
interrogates the command line. PDform0 has the statement:

   MOVE COMMAND-LINE OF POW-SELF TO MyCommandLine

Then you check MyCommandLine for whatever command line params you passed at
execution time.

For example:

PCEXAMPLE.EXE Form1

then in PCform0

MOVE COMMAND-LINE (as above)
EVALUATE COMMAND-LINE(1:5)
   WHEN "Form1"
        INVOKE POW-SELF 'CALLFORM' USING 'PCForm1'

PCform0 can be an invisible form and the above code would most likely be in
a timer event.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Fujitsu PowerCobol

- **From:** "Euromercante" <euro@dsdd.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-02T14:00:59
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<40449271$0$28120$a729d347@news.telepac.pt>`
- **References:** `<4043673d$0$28136$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <M5ydnR1VbfB5St7dRVn-uA@giganews.com>`

```
Thank you very much for you help.
Euro



"JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com> escreveu na mensagem
```

<a id="t-287ca76104"></a>
## Thread: IBM mainframe - COBOL, LE - "new hint" — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### IBM mainframe - COBOL, LE - "new hint"

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-02T07:08:22+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,ibm.software.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<GpW0c.15273$yZ1.14760@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`

```
At last week's SHARE (IBM user group) meeting,  I learned something (well one
among many things) that I thought that I would  share with comp.lang.cobol,
IBM-MAIN, some other newsgroups/fora - and will probably do an RCF on.

Non-IBM mainframe people may "ignore" this note as you will.

Bottom-Line: (starting from the conclusion)

In (new) COBOL programs that use the Local-Storage Section (in addition to - or
instead of Working-Storage)
  - Be VERY careful that you (the application programmer) initialize fields - if
you require them to have specific "initial" values.
 - do NOT think that LE STORAGE(00, ...) run-time option will set Local-Storage
items to binary zeroes (as it does for WS items)
 - do NOT specify LE STORAGE(xx,xx,00,...) run-time option to initialize
Local-Storage items - unless you want your programs to "walk" rather than run.

    ***

Background:
  IBM's (ancient) OS/VS COBOL compiler (and/or its run-time) was "real nice" and
initialized WS items to binary zeroes - when they didn't have any VALUE clause
specified.  Especially under CICS, many application RELIED on this "feature" -
even though IBM *clearly* documented that "results were unpredictable" when no
VALUE clause was specified.
   When IBM introduced VS COBOL II, many applications DIED a horrible death -
because they ASSUMED WS items with no VALUE clause would have binary zeroes.
Therefore, IBM, in a relatively early release introduced the WSCLEAR run-time
option.  UNFORTUNATELY, rather than "fix" programs relying on uninitialized
values, programmers continued (with WSCLEAR support) to "assume" binary zeroes.
  With LE and LE conforming compilers (SAA AD/Cycle COBOL/370 and later), IBM
provided the first suboption of the STORAGE run-time option to "fix" not only
COBOL, but PL/I and any other program "assuming" uninitialized data items would
have binary zeroes (or some other hex value specified by the installation - not
the application programmer).

  ...

Today (and in the future),  For several releases, IBM has supported the ISO 2002
Standard COBOL feature of "Local-Storage" (particularly useful for recursive
programming and OO - but available to ALL new programs).  Unfortunately, LE
"gets" the storage for Local-Storage NOT from the "heap" but from the "stack".
This means that the first parameter of the STORAGE run-time option has NO EFFECT
on the initial value of Local-Storage items.  Rather, it is the 3rd parameter
that can be set to "initialize" data items with no VALUE clause upon initial
access to Local-Storage.  See the "dsa-alloc-value" described at:
   http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/CEEA3140/2.3.52

What is NOT clear (or at least doesn't "hit you over the head") in that
documentation, is the fact that setting the 3rd parameter of the STORAGE
run-time option has DRAMATIC (bad) performance implications for ALL applications
running with it on. (Using the initial parameter has *some* impact, but not
significantly bad).

As the Local-Storage Section should NOT be in "common usage" in "legacy"
application, and as it is NEVER been a good habit to rely on the internal values
of data items with no VALUE clause, no NEW program should require this
performance degrading option.  On the other hand, this is a fact that many
application programmers (used to WSCLEAR and
STORAGE(00)) simply may not think about.

I suggest that you "spread the word" among programmers who use new COBOL
features - and make certain that setting that 3rd parameter of the STORAGE
run-time option (other than to NONE) be something that SysProgs resist with all
their effort.
```

#### ↳ Re: IBM mainframe - COBOL, LE - "new hint"

#### ↳ Re: COBOL Error Message Assist (MVS)

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-02T19:14:02+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<_151c.18122$aT1.4549@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<2nZZb.5239$Wq1.48@newssvr23.news.prodigy.com>`

```
FYI - I have contacted my "usually reliable" sources at IBM and they have
indicated that sometimes this is a compiler bug - and sometimes this is simply a
"too large" program.  They also told me that there are some existing APARs in
the database on the message. (I haven't checked for numbers).  The general
consensus is that 700k lines of program is probably "not a good idea" - even if
it does compile sometimes / most of the time. <G>
```

## Thread: Sort registers — 14 msgs

### Sort registers

- **From:** "Euromercante" <euro@dsdd.com>

- **Message-ID:** `<4045bded$0$9937$a729d347@news.telepac.pt>`

```
Hi,
    I�m using Fujitsu PowerCobol, indexed files and I would  like to know if
it's possible to indicate the order (ascending or descending) in one of the
fields of the key in the fd file, for example:
    03 Example.
         05 A pic 9(6).
         05 B pic 9.
         05 C pic 9.
         05 D pic x(9).
and what I want to do is something like this:
    03 Example.
         05 A pic 9(6).
         05 B pic 9 DESC.
         05 C pic 9 ASC.
         05 D pic x(9).
I�m asking this, because I don�t want to use the sort in a table, but if you
know another way of doing this it could be of a great help.

Thanks
Euro
```

```
> I�m asking this, because I don�t want to use the sort in a table, but if
you
> know another way of doing this it could be of a great help.

That is not a valid FD for an indexed file.  The key field is specified in
the SELECT. Your SELECT and FD should look something like

SELECT  foo ORGANIZATION INDEXED ACCESS RANDOM KEY IS foo-key..

FD Foo
01  Foo-record
  05   foo-key
        10 A          PIC whatever
        10 B          PIC whatever
        10 C          PIC whatever
  05  foo-rest-of-record.
        10    (other fields)

I don't understand why you'd use SORT if you are using an indexed
file...unless you want to access the data in an order other than key order.


???

MCM






If that FD is for the data
If the file is indexed, the 'order' of fields within the key is
immaterial... you access data by the entire key.

Standard COBOL does not support 'order' within
```

#### ↳ Re: Sort registers

- **From:** "JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T07:46:08-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<D9udnU0_5rwOfNjdRVn-uw@giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<4045bded$0$9937$a729d347@news.telepac.pt>`

```
Euromercante wrote:
> Hi,
>     I�m using Fujitsu PowerCobol, indexed files and I would  like to
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> if you know another way of doing this it could be of a great help.

If you're suggesting the ISAM key could look like:

(A-B-C)
000001-9-1
000001-9-2
000002-8-1
000002-7-1
000002-5-1

then the answer is no. An ISAM file's primary key must be monotonicaly
increasing without duplicates.

In your case, simply use the compliment of "B" when accessing the file and
re-complement B when used as data in the program (i.e., COMPUTE B = 9 - B).

This technique is often used with dates (yyyymmdd) when you normally want
the most recent date as the first returned entry when reading a file.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Sort registers

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T12:03:34-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0403031203.1b783e@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<4045bded$0$9937$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <D9udnU0_5rwOfNjdRVn-uw@giganews.com> <Oyl1c.14111$qA2.732797@news20.bellglobal.com>`

```
Donald Tees <donald_tees@nospam.sympatico.ca> wrote 
 
> It cannot be the primary key in a combined state and get what he wants, 
> but it can be a secondary key by simply declaring it. 
> Ascending/descending order, 

You are confused.  ASCENDING/DESCENDING are part of the SORT and the
MERGE statements and may be used with SQL, but are not part of ISAM. 
They may be in some extensions but not in Fujitsu Cobol.

You can also READ PRIOR to work in descending order on a whole key,
but the question was related to parts of a key being used one way
while others are reversed.  And READ PRIOR can be done on a primary
key.

> and whether there are duplicates allowed can simply be declared as well. 

Yes, that can be done.  

> Complimenting the data to make it works 
> sucks as a technique, in my opinion. It may be justinfied in some big 
> old mainframe with thirty billion transactions and under two seconds to 
> handle them, but as a way of fooling the indexing?

Indexes are created in a way to make accessing of data convenient and
efficient.   Having numbers in the index items that make this so is
not 'fooling' the indexing, it is just making it work.  If, for
example, I want items to be read in ascending account sequence but
descending date sequence then I make the date representation such that
it is 'days until 15th October 2173' (or whatever it is).

Now I may conveniently calculate this by subtracting the day number
since 1 Jan 1900 from 99999 but I don't see how this calculation makes
it 'suck', nor do I see that if I am not using a mainframe I must use
some other number that is not at all convenient.

Given that the index does not expect these numbers to be anything in
particular, it is not 'fooling' it to give it one number instead of
another.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Sort registers

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T13:14:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<xYF1c.30290$PY.10697@newssvr26.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<4045bded$0$9937$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <D9udnU0_5rwOfNjdRVn-uw@giganews.com> <Oyl1c.14111$qA2.732797@news20.bellglobal.com> <obKdnZ4-bN3U6dvdRVn-jw@giganews.com>`

```
"JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com> wrote in message
news:obKdnZ4-bN3U6dvdRVn-jw@giganews.com...
> Hey, I'm easy.
>
> How would you add a record to an ISAM file such that when the file is
later
> read sequentially the latest date is the first record returned?

You do not read indexed files sequentially. You can read them in key order
if you want; you can even use ACCESS DYNAMIC to allow the use of the START
and READ NEXT verbs to read in key order starting somewhere other than at
the beginning.

But as far as adding records so that when you do choose to read in key order
they come out in the order you want? That has nothing to do with file access
per se; that is totally a function of the way you build the key and/or the
way the ISAM manager allows you to define those keys.

MCM
```

```
I've clearly caused some confusion here.

It "appears" the OP thought the "sequence order" and/or "PHYSICAL
construction" of the keys associated with a key-sequenced ("isam")  file are
under the direct control of the COBOL language.

Of course, COBOL of and by itself has nothing to to with these things: COBOL
deals only with the LOGICAL construction of keys and order of retrieval.

Probably just should have said that the first time....

MCM
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Sort registers

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T12:07:59-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0403041207.26bae14c@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<4045bded$0$9937$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <D9udnU0_5rwOfNjdRVn-uw@giganews.com> <Oyl1c.14111$qA2.732797@news20.bellglobal.com> <obKdnZ4-bN3U6dvdRVn-jw@giganews.com> <xYF1c.30290$PY.10697@newssvr26.news.prodigy.com> <tZKdncWm-coEpdrd4p2dnA@giganews.com>`

```
"JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com> wrote 

> Michael Mattias wrote:

> > You do not read indexed files sequentially. You can read them in key
> > order if you want; you can even use ACCESS DYNAMIC to allow the use
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> in my COBOL manuals where it appears in conjunction with ISAM files.

You should ignore that comment from MM.  ACCESS SEQUENTIAL and READ ..
AT END .. gives identical results to ACCESS DYNAMIC and READ ... NEXT
RECORD AT END ..

Both of these give the records in key sequence order, and are 'reading
the indexed file sequentially'.

START _can_ be used on a file with ACCESS SEQUENTIAL and it does not
need to be DYNAMIC for this.

What DYNAMIC does is allow a RANDOM READ to be done on the file in
addition to allowing the file to be read sequentially.  A random read
is one in which the key value in the record is set and a READ
statement without NEXT or AT END is done.  I  always use READ .. NEXT
RECORD when doing a sequential read on a file that has ACCESS DYNAMIC,
it clarifies the difference.

Both SEQUENTIAL and DYNAMIC are useful.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Sort registers

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T12:21:17-08:00

- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0403041221.2012ddfa@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<4045bded$0$9937$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <D9udnU0_5rwOfNjdRVn-uw@giganews.com> <Oyl1c.14111$qA2.732797@news20.bellglobal.com> <obKdnZ4-bN3U6dvdRVn-jw@giganews.com>`

```
"JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com> wrote 

> How would you add a record to an ISAM file such that when the file is later
> read sequentially the latest date is the first record returned?
> 
> OPEN INPUT filename REVERSED?


       START ... FIRST KEY ... REVERSED
       READ ... PREVIOUS RECORD ..

This works for the whole key size, what was actually required was
parts to be ascending and other parts descending which can only be
done by setting appropriate values in the key.
```

#### ↳ Re: Sort registers

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T09:52:24-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0403030952.765d19e@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<4045bded$0$9937$a729d347@news.telepac.pt>`

```
"Euromercante" <euro@dsdd.com> wrote 

>     Iï¿½m using Fujitsu PowerCobol, indexed files and I would  like to know if
> it's possible to indicate the order (ascending or descending) in one of the
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
> know another way of doing this it could be of a great help.

To get part of an indexed key to be desceding you reverse the value. 
If for example the value of B will be between zero and 9 then subtract
the value from 9 and store the result in B.

If both sequences are required then an alternate key is required when
the file is created with the reversed and normal values as necessary.

I do this where I want an alternate key in descending date order.  The
date is converted to days since some point, eg Jan 1 1900 and this is
subtracted from 99999 to give the value stored in the alternate key.

This only works when you are originally writing the file, of course. 
If you are reading an existing file then, no, you cannot partially
change the order you will read the records.
```

## Thread: Read, last record appears twice — 20 msgs

### Read, last record appears twice

- **From:** Julian <whateveryousend@iwontread.net>
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T19:17:48+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c2579s$1jg$1@news.brutele.be>`

```
Hi,

I am learning Cobol and I tried to read a file that I created 
previously. The file contains 4 records.

in WSS :

77 eof pic 9 value 0.

PROCEDURE DIVISION.

PGM.
	OPEN INPUT myfile.
	PERFORM READFILE UNTIL eof = 1.
	CLOSE myfile.
	STOP RUN.

READFILE.
	READ myfile-rec AT END MOVE 1 TO eof.
	DISPLAY myfile-rec.

There is no error while compiling the source code and the program is 
running well. BUT the last record of "myfile" appears twice at the 
screen. I guess that's a beginner error, but I have honestly no clue 
where the error is.

Thanks all. I hope you understand. (i speak french actually)

Julian
```

```

:>> :>	READ myfile-rec AT END MOVE 1 TO eof.
:>> :>	DISPLAY myfile-rec.
 
:>> :>There is no error while compiling the source code and the program is 
:>> :>running well. BUT the last record of "myfile" appears twice at the 
:>> :>screen. I guess that's a beginner error, but I have honestly no clue 
:>> :>where the error is.
 
:>> Try walking thru the program, i.e., get a copy of the file and pretend to be
:>> the computer and interpret the instructions one by one.
 
:>> Your error will be clear.

:>I runned thru and I've seen that when the "AT END MOVE 1 TO eof" is 
:>evaluated, the DISPLAY below is executed as well. Cobol does not 
:>consider the last record of the file as the EOF, isn't it ? Cobol 
:>consider that I've reached the EOF when it does not find a record 
:>after the last record of my file.

Yes.

The EOF condition occurs when a read is attempted and there aren't any more
records.

You have two approaches:

The old fashioned way - do a priming read and do the read at the end of the
perform.

The scope way - use a NOT AT END clause.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Read, last record appears twice

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T19:25:42+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Wiq1c.30016$PY.14186@newssvr26.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<c2579s$1jg$1@news.brutele.be> <2j8c409mhvvh0qbvi37fkdbp90crh1ld98@4ax.com> <c258tr$375$1@news.brutele.be>`

```
"Julian" <whateveryousend@iwontread.net> wrote in message
news:c258tr$375$1@news.brutele.be...
> I runned thru and I've seen that when the "AT END MOVE 1 TO eof" is
> evaluated, the DISPLAY below is executed as well. Cobol does not
> consider the last record of the file as the EOF, isn't it ? Cobol
> consider that I've reached the EOF when it does not find a record
> after the last record of my file.

Actually, all COBOL and AFAIK any language product will state that the
contents of a file buffer are "undefined" if the last READ was not a valid
read; and a READ which results in the AT END condition is not a valid read.

So, what you displayed "just happened" to be the record put in the buffer on
the last valid read. Next time you run the program, though, that may not be
true.

(Further hint: see the NOT AT END clause of the READ verb).

MCM
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Read, last record appears twice

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T19:46:41+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<BCq1c.17520$yZ1.3130@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<c2579s$1jg$1@news.brutele.be> <2j8c409mhvvh0qbvi37fkdbp90crh1ld98@4ax.com> <c258tr$375$1@news.brutele.be> <Wiq1c.30016$PY.14186@newssvr26.news.prodigy.com>`

```
Michael,
  I know that what you say is NOT true if you use the "SAME RECORD AREA" clause.
I am not certain, but I *think* that it may not be true for "normal" OPEN INPUT
sequential files.  According to the ISO 2002 Standard (and I think this is the
same as earlier standards),

"9.1.2 Record area
The record area is a storage area associated with a file in which logical
records from that file are made accessible to a runtime element. The record area
is made accessible to the runtime element at the completion of a successfully
executed OPEN statement. For files open in the input mode, the logical record is
available in the record area after execution of a successful read. For files
open in the extend or output mode, the logical record is available until
execution of a successful write or rewrite. For files open in the I-O mode, the
logical record is available after execution of a successful read until the
execution of either a read or successful rewrite."

I believe that the record area is available *and* defined after an AT END
condition (assuming there was a preceeding successful READ) - but becomes
unavailable during the CLOSE.  I could be mistaken on this - but I didn't find
anything (quickly) that says otherwise.

Thane or Chuck - if you are "watching" do you know if there is a rule on this
('85 or 2002 Standard)?
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Read, last record appears twice

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T17:01:15-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0403031701.50ff44b8@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<c2579s$1jg$1@news.brutele.be> <2j8c409mhvvh0qbvi37fkdbp90crh1ld98@4ax.com> <c258tr$375$1@news.brutele.be> <Wiq1c.30016$PY.14186@newssvr26.news.prodigy.com> <BCq1c.17520$yZ1.3130@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`

```
"William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com> wrote 

> For files open in the input mode, the logical record is
> available in the record area after execution of a successful read.

When the AT END is followed it is an 'unsuccessful READ', ie the File
status will not indicate 'success' with a '0' in the first position,
in fact it will have '1'.

> ... the
> logical record is available after execution of a successful read until the
> execution of either a read or successful rewrite."
 
> I believe that the record area is available *and* defined after an AT END
> condition (assuming there was a preceeding successful READ) 

The record _area_ is available until after a successful CLOSE.  The
content of the area (ie the logical record) is only defined after a
successful READ and is undefined after a successful WRITE or REWRITE
or after an unsuccessful operation.  A READ that takes the AT END
branch is unsuccessful.

> - but becomes unavailable during the CLOSE. 

Unavailability is irrelevant and was not part of the problem. You are
confused. When the standard states "the logical record is available"
it is saying that the data items are defined and is not referring to
the availablity of the buffer.

I do know that some IBMers think that the buffer becomes unavailable
after an AT END, but that was a fault in their system many years ago,
not an issue with Cobol.
```

```
docdwarf@panix.com wrote 

> >Published standards and rules aside, I think it totally foolish to rely on
> >the contents of a file buffer except following a sucessful READ.

It is also worth noting that a record buffer is undefined after a
successful or a failed WRITE or REWRITE.  I have used systems (decades
ago) where the record buffer was used by the system to hold displaced
records from overflow areas.  In some circumstances the program would
report that the record failed to be written due to overflow areas
being full.  The actual record being written was actually on the disk
but a _different_ record was now in the record area and it was this
displaced one, which may have been in the file for some time, that was
now no longer in the file.

Even after a successful write the record area may have been a
different record.
 
> 'Rules aside', indeed... a rule I was taught was 'Thou Shalt Not Mess With 
> File Areas, Nor Shalt Thou Code READ Without INTO nor WRITE without FROM'.

That mainly comes from IBM sites where there were other problems.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Read, last record appears twice

- **From:** l.willms@jpberlin.de (Lueko Willms)
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T19:27:00+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<94BsIXp9flB@jpberlin-l.willms.jpberlin.de>`
- **References:** `<c2579s$1jg$1@news.brutele.be> <2j8c409mhvvh0qbvi37fkdbp90crh1ld98@4ax.com> <c258tr$375$1@news.brutele.be>`

```
     Am  03.03.04
schrieb  whateveryousend@iwontread.net (Julian)
    auf  /COMP/LANG/COBOL
     in  c258tr$375$1@news.brutele.be
  ueber  Re: Read, last record appears twice

w> I runned thru and I've seen that when the "AT END MOVE 1 TO eof" is
w> evaluated, the DISPLAY below is executed as well. Cobol does not
w> consider the last record of the file as the EOF, isn't it ? Cobol
w> consider that I've reached the EOF when it does not find a record
w> after the last record of my file.

  Right.

  The best way to do your example would be like this:

        OPEN INPUT myfile.
        READ myfile-rec AT END MOVE 1 TO eof.
        PERFORM UNTIL eof = 1
          DISPLAY myfile-rec
          READ myfile-rec AT END MOVE 1 TO eof
        END-PERFORM.
        CLOSE myfile.
        STOP RUN.



    It would be even more cute when you add a condition-name to your  
77-level variable "eof", like this:

   77 eof pic 9 value 0.
   88 Is-at-EOF VALUE 1.

    and then your routine could look like this:

    MAIN SECTION.
    START-HERE.
        OPEN INPUT myfile.
        READ myfile-rec AT END SET Is-at-EOF TO TRUE.
        PERFORM   UNTIL Is-at-EOF
          DISPLAY myfile-rec
          READ myfile-rec AT END SET Is-at-EOF TO TRUE
        END-PERFORM.
        CLOSE myfile.
    THE-END.
        STOP RUN.



Yours,
Lï¿½ko Willms                                     http://www.mlwerke.de
/--------- L.WILLMS@jpberlin.de -- Alle Rechte vorbehalten --

"Die Arbeit in weiï¿½er Haut kann sich nicht dort emanzipieren, wo sie
in schwarzer Haut gebrandmarkt wird."     - Karl Marx     12.11.1866
```

```
The AT END doesn't occur at the last record read, it occurs at the NEXT record
after that, which doesn't exist.

The way I would structure your code is like this:

> 	OPEN INPUT myfile.
> 	READ myfile-rec AT END MOVE 1 TO eof.
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> 	READ myfile-rec AT END MOVE 1 TO eof.

What happens here is that only if eof is not = 1 that the display occurs.
```

#### ↳ Re: Read, last record appears twice

- **From:** LX-i <lxi0007@netscape.net>
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T19:07:05-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<104d09d410igpa0@corp.supernews.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<c2579s$1jg$1@news.brutele.be>`
- **References:** `<c2579s$1jg$1@news.brutele.be>`

```
Julian wrote:
> Hi,
> 
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
>     OPEN INPUT myfile.
                  ^^^^^^
>     PERFORM READFILE UNTIL eof = 1.
>     CLOSE myfile.
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>     READ myfile-rec AT END MOVE 1 TO eof.
            ^^^^^^^^^^
>     DISPLAY myfile-rec.

If your compiler lets that through, they're being generous.  Generally 
speaking, you read a file, and write a record.

Try placing that display within a "Not at End" clause...

Read myfile
   at End
     Move 1 to EOF
   Not at End
     Display myfile-Rec
End-Read.

Of course, you could do more than one thing within each of these clauses 
- that's the purpose the End-Read serves.  It's not required (unless 
you're doing this inside some sort of conditional statement, such as a 
"When" or an "If" statement, or an inline perform, which I'll show 
below), but it does tend to block the code so it guides the eyes nicely. 
  (That last bit is my opinion...)

Anyway, about the inline perform - it, combined with the "not at end" 
clause, will allow you to do all this in one paragraph.

Pgm.
     Open Input myfile
     Perform Until EOF = 1
         Read myfile
           at End
             Move 1 to EOF
           Not at End
             Display myfile-rec
         End-Read
     End-Perform
     Close myfile
     Stop Run.

Hope that helps - COBOL is a pretty easy language to pick up, and there 
are some really great things it can do.  It's also flexible - there are 
several ways to code what you've tried to do in this simple program.  :)
```

#### ↳ Re: Read, last record appears twice

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<MsudnVjtq6tGXdrdRVn-iQ@comcast.com>`
- **References:** `<c2579s$1jg$1@news.brutele.be>`

```
Try
If eof not = 1 DISPLAY myfile-rec.
```

<a id="t-44df99e427"></a>
## Thread: LE Condition Handlers with COBOL in the run-unit — 2 msgs

### LE Condition Handlers with COBOL in the run-unit

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T19:53:58+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,ibm.software.cobol,ibm.software.le
- **Message-ID:** `<qJq1c.17526$yZ1.9652@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`

```
Another "follow-up" to a discussion at last week's SHARE meeting.

*IF* you are using LE condition handlers (and/or the CEE3SRC or CEE3GRC callable
services), you may be interested in the following RCF (Reader's Comment Form)
that I just submitted - correcting some of the current (conflicting) LE
documentation.

   ***
The USAGE note information at the bottom of this note should be added in (at
least) two places in the LE documentation. See:
http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/CEEA3140/3.5.15.1

and

http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/CEEA3140/3.5.5.1

The section at:

http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/ceea2140/3.1.4.2.2

which is NOT reflected in the LE Reference Manual should be replaced with the
corrected information and this should be "coordinated with" the COBOL example
at:

http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/ceea3140/3.5.5.3

which currently is totally the OPPOSITE of the Programming Guide.

Finally, the COBOL documentation at:

http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/igy3pg20/4.2.4.1

and

http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/igy3pg20/8.2.2.2

and

http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/igy3lr20/1.3.8.6?DT

should also be updated.

***

Correct information follows (word-smithing is probably needed):

When any COBOL program calls any LE callable service, the COBOL Return-Code
special register is set to zero (regardless of whether or not the callable
service was successfully executed). Similarly, when a COBOL program calls any
other non-COBOL subroutine (whether user-written or vendor supplied), the
return-code special register reflects whatever is in R15 of the called
subprogram. See the warnings at:

http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/igy3pg20/3.1.1.7

and

http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/igy3pg20/3.2.1.4

Therefore, if your LE Enclave has a COBOL program as its main program and an LE
condition handler may (or may not) have been activated within the run-unit, it
is important that immediately before your STOP RUN or GOBACK statement (in the
main COBOL program) that you make an explicit call to the CEE3GRC callable
service and move the resulting Enclave Return-Code to the COBOL RETURN-CODE
special register. If your application may have explicitly set the RETURN-CODE
special register, then you should also use the CEE3SRC callable service to set
the value in the LE Enclave Return-Register; otherwise this value may be
overwritten by a final call to CEE3GRC before the GOBACK or Stop Run statement
and/or the return-code value will not be percolated to non-COBOL LE conforming
main programs.
```

<a id="t-d7e858daf8"></a>

<a id="t-66b96f71a9"></a>
## Thread: Please test this recursive quicksort — 1 msgs

### Please test this recursive quicksort

- **From:** ggrotz73@hotmail.com (Sky_Eagle1)
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T19:43:30-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b305dd6.0403031943.5b2e6cd@posting.google.com>`

```
I did this on the Fujitsu cobol compiler, because I don't have access
to IBM LE COBOL.  I was wondering if someone could test this and see
if it works?  I got all the compile errors out of it, but the version
of the COBOL compiler I have doesn't allow recursive subcalls in it's
execs so I can't test it.

Hope this is interesting to someone...I'm kind of doing different
things you don't normally see in COBOL just to see if they could be
done...

The main program
 CBL NOSSRANGE
 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
 PROGRAM-ID. QSRTMAIN.
*++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++
* QUICKSORT (RECURSIVE?) MAIN PROGRAM.
* CREDIT "Sky_Eagle1 on comp.lang.cobol"
*++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++
 ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
 DATA DIVISION.
 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.

 01  SORT-TABLE-ITEMS.
     04  SORT-TABLE       PIC 9(5) OCCURS 1000 TIMES
                          INDEXED BY INTERVAL-LEFT INTERVAL-RIGHT.
 01  TABLE-LEFT           INDEX.
 01  TABLE-RIGHT          INDEX.

 01  TEST-VARS.
     04  IN-TIME          PIC 9(8).
     04  GEN-COUNTER      PIC S9(5) COMP-3.
     04  COUNTER-1        PIC S9(5) COMP-3.
     04  COUNTER-2        PIC S9(5) COMP-3.

*----------------------------------------------------------------
 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
 0000-START-SECTION.
     ACCEPT IN-TIME FROM TIME.
     DISPLAY "BEFORE: " IN-TIME.
     PERFORM VARYING GEN-COUNTER FROM 1 BY 1 UNTIL GEN-COUNTER > 1000
        MOVE 1 TO COUNTER-1
        PERFORM VARYING COUNTER-2 FROM 1000
               BY -1 UNTIL COUNTER-2 < 1
           MOVE COUNTER-2 TO SORT-TABLE (COUNTER-1)
           ADD 1 TO COUNTER-1
        END-PERFORM
        SET INTERVAL-LEFT TO 1
        SET INTERVAL-RIGHT TO 1000
        SET TABLE-LEFT TO INTERVAL-LEFT
        SET TABLE-RIGHT TO INTERVAL-RIGHT
        CALL "QSORT5" USING SORT-TABLE-ITEMS TABLE-LEFT TABLE-RIGHT
     END-PERFORM.
     ACCEPT IN-TIME FROM TIME.
     DISPLAY "AFTER: " IN-TIME.
     PERFORM 0600-DISPLAY.
     GOBACK.

 0600-DISPLAY SECTION.
     PERFORM VARYING GEN-COUNTER FROM 1 BY 1 UNTIL GEN-COUNTER > 1000
        DISPLAY GEN-COUNTER ': ' SORT-TABLE (GEN-COUNTER)
     END-PERFORM.

The subroutine

CBL NOSSRANGE
 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
 PROGRAM-ID. QSORT5. RECURSIVE.
*++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++
* QUICKSORT RECURSIVE SUBPROGRAM.
* CREDIT "Sky_Eagle1 at comp.lang.cobol"
*++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++
 ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
 DATA DIVISION.
 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
  01  SORT-PROC-VARS.
      04  TEMP-SWAP-VALUE  PIC 9(5).
      04  INTERVAL-PIVOT   PIC 9(5).
      04  INDEX-T1         INDEX.
      04  INDEX-T2         INDEX.

 LINKAGE SECTION.
  01  SORT-TABLE-ITEMS.
      04  SORT-TABLE       PIC 9(5) OCCURS 1000 TIMES
                           INDEXED BY INTERVAL-LEFT
                                      INTERVAL-RIGHT
                                      SWEEP-LEFT
                                      SWEEP-RIGHT.
  01  TABLE-LEFT       INDEX.
  01  TABLE-RIGHT      INDEX.

*----------------------------------------------------------------
 PROCEDURE DIVISION USING SORT-TABLE-ITEMS TABLE-LEFT TABLE-RIGHT.
 0000-START-SECTION.
     IF TABLE-LEFT < TABLE-RIGHT
        SET SWEEP-LEFT TO TABLE-LEFT
        MOVE SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-LEFT) TO INTERVAL-PIVOT
        SET SWEEP-LEFT UP BY 1
        SET SWEEP-RIGHT TO TABLE-RIGHT
        PERFORM 2100-SHIFT-INTERVAL UNTIL SWEEP-LEFT > SWEEP-RIGHT
        MOVE SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-RIGHT) TO SORT-TABLE (INTERVAL-LEFT)
        MOVE INTERVAL-PIVOT TO SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-RIGHT)
        SET SWEEP-RIGHT DOWN BY 1
        SET INDEX-T1 TO SWEEP-RIGHT
        SET INDEX-T2 TO SWEEP-LEFT
        CALL "QSORT5" USING SORT-TABLE-ITEMS TABLE-LEFT INDEX-T1
        CALL "QSORT5" USING SORT-TABLE-ITEMS INDEX-T2 TABLE-RIGHT
     END-IF.
     GOBACK.

 2100-SHIFT-INTERVAL SECTION.      
     PERFORM UNTIL (SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-LEFT) <= INTERVAL-PIVOT)
         SET SWEEP-LEFT UP BY 1
     END-PERFORM.      
     PERFORM UNTIL (SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-RIGHT) > INTERVAL-PIVOT)
        SET SWEEP-RIGHT DOWN BY 1
     END-PERFORM.      
     IF SWEEP-LEFT < SWEEP-RIGHT         
        MOVE SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-RIGHT) TO TEMP-SWAP-VALUE
        MOVE SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-LEFT) TO SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-RIGHT)
        MOVE TEMP-SWAP-VALUE TO SORT-TABLE (SWEEP-LEFT)
     END-IF.
```

## Thread: Performance in perform loops — 3 this month / 21 total

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax)_

_Thread started [2004-01](2004-01.md#t-1175f92a08)._

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Performance in perform loops

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** ggrotz73@hotmail.com (Sky_Eagle1)
- **Date:** 2004-03-03T20:09:31-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b305dd6.0403032009.7660b91f@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<e224fa77.0401280245.1fd41f48@posting.google.com> <naKdnYuz8smKmoTdRVn-uQ@giganews.com> <qdbSb.12657$oN3.5870@newssvr24.news.prodigy.com> <Iaednatqpp4xAYTdRVn-tA@giganews.com> <e224fa77.0401300657.69af4f36@posting.google.com> <BzASb.3777$F23.1956@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <bvlsq6$i2q$1@peabody.colorado.edu>`

```
Looking at this code, a few things jump out at me.  The table you are
processing is huge.  I would look at it and consider whether there's
another way to get around having such a big table in memory.

Furthermore, when you consider loops, they can and will be the major
amount of processing.  Also, remember any small coding problem will be
magnified 100 fold so it pays to optimize it.  This means simplify
simplify simplify...the fewest instructions to do the job...

The first thought that comes out other than the table size and all the
paging to virtual memory the system must be doing to handle that is
data conversions.  Make sure every move and comparison in that loop
are with like variables.  Comparing unlike variables (say PIC S9(4)
binary and PIC S9(3) COMP-3) require type conversions to do that,
which is extra cpu time, since it will have to do that each time
through your loop.  One example has already been pointed out to you
(the comparisons of abg-ind and abg-end) and I would point out the
rest if there are any but you don't post variable definitions for all
of the variables you use.  For ABG-END make sure it is an INDEX type,
as an example...

The second thought I had, which it seems you do do is make sure all
table access is indexed.  I remember hearing a case in school with TWA
where they had a program run 24+ hrs and then cut it down to 4 hours
simply by coding for indexed access.

The third thought I had is to truly think through your logic and try
to decouple some of it from the loops - if you can do that that will
help tremendously on your speed.  Basically anything you can get out
of those perform loops and into an iterative cycle will help you.  I'm
looking at your code for that and will probably post something if I
can think of it.

Hope this helps some.

Original post:
Hello, I am looking for some tips in order to improve the performance
of the following COBOL code. Our investigation has shown, that the
section C032 is the most time consuming part of the whole program.
We spend more than 60% of the cpu time in the simple perform loops of
the 'C032-PRUEFE-BEDG' section.
<clipped>
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Performance in perform loops

_(thread depth: 8)_

- **From:** ggrotz73@hotmail.com (Sky_Eagle1)
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T19:55:30-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b305dd6.0403041955.6f2ca67f@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<e224fa77.0401280245.1fd41f48@posting.google.com> <naKdnYuz8smKmoTdRVn-uQ@giganews.com> <qdbSb.12657$oN3.5870@newssvr24.news.prodigy.com> <Iaednatqpp4xAYTdRVn-tA@giganews.com> <e224fa77.0401300657.69af4f36@posting.google.com> <BzASb.3777$F23.1956@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <bvlsq6$i2q$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <b305dd6.0403032009.7660b91f@posting.google.com>`

```
OK some more since I thought about this...

The first quoted statement comes true in your code.  You will want to
check the code very carefully for things that are getting run all the
time that probably shouldn't...but some specific things I've seen...

IF  WS-VFELD   NOT < TB-ABG-ABGRVON (ABG-IND)
   AND WS-VFELD   NOT > TB-ABG-ABGRBIS (ABG-IND)

I'm not sure if there's specific reasons for logic like this occurring
in your code, or which would be more efficient, but I'm a big opponent
of using negative logic, just because it's not as understandable. 
Something like this would be preferable to me, but it's always worth
seeing an assembler list to make sure you're not hurting efficiency.

IF  WS-VFELD >= TB-ABG-ABGRVON (ABG-IND)
   AND WS-VFELD <= TB-ABG-ABGRBIS (ABG-IND)

Then it helps to simplify things.  Inline performs can get confusing
and make it hard so you can see what is going on in your code.  I
would suggest trying to take some of the inline performs and make them
into separate paragraphs, so your logic becomes clearer to you.  If
you do that you will see that the following is getting performed as
part of a loop.

PERFORM UNTIL BLA BLA
IF WS-FORMAT = 'X'
   IF  WS-VFELD >= TB-ABG-ABGRVON (ABG-IND)
       AND WS-VFELD <= TB-ABG-ABGRBIS (ABG-IND)
            SET PS-TREFFER-JA TO TRUE
   END-IF
ELSE
   IF  WS-VFELD-N >= TB-ABG-ABGRVON-N(ABG-IND)
       AND WS-VFELD-N <= TB-ABG-ABGRBIS-N(ABG-IND)
          SET PS-TREFFER-JA TO TRUE
   END-IF
END-IF
SET  ABG-IND UP BY 1
END-PERFORM.

What I mean by decoupling the code is that we can rewrite things more
efficiently to move logic OUT of the perform loop.  This logic is hard
to see, but becomes clear once you set things out as separate
paragraphs.  Compare the code up top with this code...

IF WS-FORMAT = 'X'
   PERFORM UNTIL BLA BLA
      IF  WS-VFELD >= TB-ABG-ABGRVON (ABG-IND)
           AND WS-VFELD <= TB-ABG-ABGRBIS (ABG-IND)
                SET PS-TREFFER-JA TO TRUE
      END-IF
      SET  ABG-IND UP BY 1
   END-PERFORM
ELSE
   PERFORM UNTIL BLA BLA
     IF  WS-VFELD-N >= TB-ABG-ABGRVON-N(ABG-IND)
         AND WS-VFELD-N <= TB-ABG-ABGRBIS-N(ABG-IND)
            SET PS-TREFFER-JA TO TRUE
     END-IF
     SET  ABG-IND UP BY 1
   END-PERFORM
END-IF.

What is important to remember is that more lines of code does not
always equal more processing time.  This is a big fallacy that most
coders have, and becomes apparent here.  While yes the same logic is
being expressed in more lines of code, the code I posted will be more
efficient.  Why?  Look at the first code.  The "IF WS-FORMAT = 'X'"
question is being asked EVERY time the loop is entered.  In the
rewritten code, the question is only asked ONCE before the loop is
even entered.  In rewriting this code for your application we reduced
the number of comparisons by 399999.  I noticed as well that other
code that you posted may be decoupled as well.

Hope this helps you, if you still are watching.  Reply if you have
questions...or for anyone, let's talk about program optimization.

ggrotz73@hotmail.com (Sky_Eagle1) wrote in message news:<b305dd6.0403032009.7660b91f@posting.google.com>...
> Also, remember any small coding problem will be
> magnified 100 fold so it pays to optimize it.  This means simplify
> simplify simplify...the fewest instructions to do the job...

> to decouple some of it from the loops - if you can do that that will
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> can think of it.
```

- **From:** "Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

- **References:** `<e224fa77.0401280245.1fd41f48@posting.google.com> <naKdnYuz8smKmoTdRVn-uQ@giganews.com> <qdbSb.12657$oN3.5870@newssvr24.news.prodigy.com> <Iaednatqpp4xAYTdRVn-tA@giganews.com> <e224fa77.0401300657.69af4f36@posting.google.com> <BzASb.3777$F23.1956@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <bvlsq6$i2q$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <b305dd6.0403032009.7660b91f@posting.google.com> <b305dd6.0403041955.6f2ca67f@posting.google.com>`

```
On  4-Mar-2004, ggrotz73@hotmail.com (Sky_Eagle1) wrote:

> IF  WS-VFELD   NOT < TB-ABG-ABGRVON (ABG-IND)
>    AND WS-VFELD   NOT > TB-ABG-ABGRBIS (ABG-IND)
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>    AND WS-VFELD <= TB-ABG-ABGRBIS (ABG-IND)

I'm a big proponent of the ELSE clause

IF WS-VFELD < TB-ABG-ABGRVON (ABG-IND)
OR WS-VFELD > TB-ABG-ABGRVON (ABG-IND)
     CONTINUE
ELSE
      PERFORM WITHIN-RANGE
END-IF
```

<a id="t-44a4758717"></a>
## Thread: IF... (imperative) Not Necessarily So — 12 msgs

### IF... (imperative) Not Necessarily So

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T11:56:06-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c27n36$h00$1@panix5.panix.com>`

```

Learn something new every day, it seems... and so I post it here to show 
everyone how little I actually know.

(note - all compiler references are to IBM mainframe software)

I was taught the syntax of IF (condition) [THEN] (imperative statement)... 
and the compiler enforced this fairly well; even the venerable IKFCBL00 
would throw a condition code of 12 on

IF FLD1 = ZEROES.

... and this holds for the IBM Enterprise COBOL for z/OS and OS/390 3.2.0 
which I presently use at work; it returns

IGYPS2079-S   Expected a verb or "NEXT SENTENCE", but found ". ". 

This syntax holds true for those who employ scope-delimiters, as well, as

IF FLD1 = ZEROES
END-IF

... with or without a period (full stop) following the END-IF generates

IGYPS2079-S   Expected a verb or "NEXT SENTENCE", but found "END-IF".

... as, some might argue, Well It Should Be.

However... I was given a chunk of code to modify, the scenario being that 
they no longer wanted records with zeroes in a couple of fields.  At first 
I was told that if the second field was zeroes the sign-indicator (a 
separate alpha field preceding the numeric field... no SIGN LEADING 
SEPARATE CHARACTER here!) should be blanked out since the indicator was 
initialised to '+' in another section.  The output records were stored in 
a WORKING STORAGE table and the code started out as:

     PERFORM 9798-WRITE-DETREC THRU 9798-EX
      VARYING SUB03 FROM 1 BY 1             
       UNTIL SUB03 > 14.                    
...

 9798-WRITE-DETREC.                                    
*                                                  
     WRITE OUT-REC FROM WK-REC (SUB03).         
     ADD 1  TO  OUT-COUNT.                         
*                                                       
 9798-EX.                                               
     EXIT.                                              

So... I coded the following:

 9798-WRITE-DETREC.                                    
*                                                       
     IF (WK-FLD1 (SUB03) = ZEROES)           
         IF (WK-FLD2 (SUB03) = ZEROES)         
             GO TO 9798-EX                              
         END-IF                                         
         MOVE SPACES  TO  WK-FLD2-SIGN (SUB03)   
     END-IF.                                            
*                                                  
     WRITE OUT-REC FROM WK-REC (SUB03).         
     ADD 1  TO  OUT-COUNT.                         
*                                                       
 9798-EX.                                               
     EXIT.                                              

... and ran the job and submitted the test-results for examination.  I 
then received the classic 'I know that's what we told you but it's not 
what we want...'; seems that they wanted the second '+' back again because 
it made it easier to eyeball the unformatted data... but I've been burned 
by 'Take it out... put it back... now take it out again' before so I 
changed a single character to make it:

 9798-WRITE-DETREC.                                    
*                                                       
     IF (WK-FLD1 (SUB03) = ZEROES)           
         IF (WK-FLD2 (SUB03) = ZEROES)         
             GO TO 9798-EX                              
         END-IF                                         
*        MOVE SPACES  TO  WK-FLD2-SIGN (SUB03)   
     END-IF.                                            
*                                                  
     WRITE OUT-REC FROM WK-REC (SUB03).         
     ADD 1  TO  OUT-COUNT.                         
*                                                       
 9798-EX.                                               
     EXIT.                                              

Now... as I read the above the the GO TO is predicated upon a second-level 
conditional... but there is *nothing* predicated on the first.

And yet... it compiles and runs and does just what I want.

DD
```

#### ↳ Re: IF... (imperative) Not Necessarily So

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T18:29:29+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<dAK1c.19044$yZ1.7876@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<c27n36$h00$1@panix5.panix.com>`

```
Your nested IF ... END-IF *is* an imperative statement (scope terminated
conditional statement) and as such THAT is  the "action" taken by your outermost
IF.  This is just the same as:

  IF A = "A"
     Add 1 to X
         On size error
              Display "here"
     End-Add
 End-If

or (using another scope terminated conditional)

 IF A = "A"
    Evaluate X
       When "Y"
           Display "HERE"
    End-Evaluate
End-IF
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: IF... (imperative) Not Necessarily So

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T13:43:19-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c27tc7$2dk$1@panix5.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<c27n36$h00$1@panix5.panix.com> <dAK1c.19044$yZ1.7876@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`

```
In article <dAK1c.19044$yZ1.7876@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>,
William M. Klein <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com> wrote:
>Your nested IF ... END-IF *is* an imperative statement (scope terminated
>conditional statement) and as such THAT is  the "action" taken by your outermost
>IF.

I know that an inner IF is predicated by the outer, Mr Klein... what I 
find unusual is that the inner IF has no associated imperative.  It is as 
though I wrote:

IF COND-1
    IF COND-2
    END-IF
    DISPLAY 'COND-1'
END-IF

> This is just the same as:
>
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> End-If

Not as I read it... my code is analagous to

If A = 'A'
   Add 1 to X
        On size error
   End-Add
End-If

>
>or (using another scope terminated conditional)
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>End-IF

Likewise, no... in my code the 'MOVE SPACES' is commented out (sorry for
not having made that more clear) so in this case it would be:

If A = 'A'
    Evaluate X
        When 'Y'
    End-Evaluate
End-If

DD

><docdwarf@panix.com> wrote in message news:c27n36$h00$1@panix5.panix.com...
>>
…[94 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

#### ↳ Re: IF... (imperative) Not Necessarily So

- **From:** LX-i <lxi0007@netscape.net>
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T18:38:29-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<104fj0bag3vu51@corp.supernews.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<c27n36$h00$1@panix5.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<c27n36$h00$1@panix5.panix.com>`

```
docdwarf@panix.com wrote:
>  9798-WRITE-DETREC.                                    
> *                                                       
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
> And yet... it compiles and runs and does just what I want.

Nothing wrong with that at all...  There is at lease -one- imperative 
within that.  You could have just as easily said

IF    (WK-FLD1 (SUB03) = ZEROES)
   AND (WK-FLD2 (SUB03) = ZEROES)
     GO TO 9798-EX
END-IF.

I've seen that many times in code at my job...  People add conditions, 
and don't stop to think that they could "And" them together.  It looks 
something like

IF EQPP-TYPE = 'A'
    IF EQPP-SRD (1:1) = 'X'
       IF SRD-MDS = '  F0119011'
          MOVE 58 TO REJCDE
          GO TO TRANS-END.

Technically, there are no imperatives on the first 2, but as you've 
seen, it works.  :)
```

<a id="t-bc3b001dfc"></a>
## Thread: use of CLOSE UNIT FOR REMOVAL — 8 msgs

### use of CLOSE UNIT FOR REMOVAL

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T11:27:05-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c27sds$1q6m0m$1@ID-184804.news.uni-berlin.de>`

```
First, the COBOL in question here is COBOL for VSE/ESA.  I'm guessing it
also applies to other IBM mainframe COBOLs such as Enterprise COBOL (for
z/OS), but perhaps not.

History: We have several COBOL jobs that read 1 or more tapes that are in
the same format (NACHA format, Visa Base II format, etc.).  On some days
there is only one tape, some days two, some days three etc.  Most of our
program do something like this (some of this is pseudo-COBOL):

OPEN INPUT TAPE-FILE
READ AND PROCESS TAPE-FILE UNTIL END OF FILE
CLOSE TAPE-FILE
ASK OPERATOR "Is there another tape?"
if YES,  tell operator "eject tape and then answer 'yes' to continue.  when
operator answers we loop back to the top.
if NO end program

I (and the operators) have long wished that COBOL itself could eject the
tape.

Somewhere (and it's been a while so I don't recall where) I came upon the
knowledge that using the statement "CLOSE file-name UNIT FOR REMOVAL" will
eject the tape *without* actually closing the file.  See the following
example:

OPEN INPUT TAPE-FILE
READ TAPE-FILE
CLOSE TAPE-FILE UNIT FOR REMOVAL
READ TAPE-FILE
CLOSE TAPE-FILE UNIT FOR REMOVAL
READ TAPE-FILE
CLOSE TAPE-FILE WITH LOCK

What this would do is open tape 1, read a record on tape 1, eject tape 1,
read a record on tape 2 (once tape 2 is loaded), eject tape 2, read a record
on tape 3 (once tape 3 is loaded), eject tape 3 and quit.

This seems to work fine.  The problem is reading the tape until the
end-of-file condition is met.  Once the EOF condition is met, while I can
close it for removal and it ejects the tape my next read returns with status
code '46' ("preceding READ statement caused an at end condition").

This both does and does not make sense.  It makes sense in that the error
it's giving is accurate.  However I still want to be able to do what I want
to do, which is reach the end of 1 tape, eject that tape, have a new tape
loaded and continue processing.

Now in the case of the file formats I am looking at there is a trailer
record.  I am able to set an EOF field to true once I've read the trailer
record but prior to attempting another read.  By doing this I can avoid
triggering the actual "at end" condition.  This allows my program to work as
desired.  But it still bugs me!  It seems to me that doing the CLOSE UNIT
FOR REMOVAL should reset the "at end" condition to no longer be true.

Any thoughts?  Do other COBOLs work this way?  Am I just being anal, since I
already know a work-around?


--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA
```

#### ↳ Re: use of CLOSE UNIT FOR REMOVAL

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T18:54:19+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<vXK1c.19067$yZ1.5821@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<c27sds$1q6m0m$1@ID-184804.news.uni-berlin.de>`

```
Frank,
  As you know, I know just enough about VSE to get myself in trouble.
Furthermore, I explicitly remember there being a LOT of  "issues" about REMOVAL
and REWIND with COBOL on VSE (differences between DOS/VS COBOL and - I think -
VS COBOL II - also VSE working differently than MVS).

HOWEVER, without knowing your exact application needs, it sounds to me as if you
should be able to code a

   USE AFTER STANDARD ENDING REEL LABEL PROCESSING

DECLARATIVE to accomplish what you want.

See:
  http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/igyvr002/8.1.15.3


In the declarative, you could "ask" the operator if there was another tape or
not - if not simply CLOSE the file - if SO - do NOT close the file but simply
try another READ and it should call for the mount of the next reel.

Am I missing something?

P.S.  Check the IBM "archives" for APARs related to CLOSE REWIND or REMOVAL on
VSE.  They may be VERY old - but I think they may help you understand exactly
what is (or is supposed to be) happening.
```

#### ↳ Re: use of CLOSE UNIT FOR REMOVAL

- **From:** mircea_tamas@yahoo.com (mircea)
- **Date:** 2004-03-07T07:27:29-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<5f25b5cf.0403070727.77973034@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<c27sds$1q6m0m$1@ID-184804.news.uni-berlin.de>`

```
Frank

your problem seems to mirror my problem about "Tape load/unload from
within a Cobol/MVS program" at
http://groups.google.com/groups?hl=en&lr=&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&threadm=5f25b5cf.0301230204.71170b4c%40posting.google.com&rnum=1&prev=/groups%3Fhl%3Den%26lr%3D%26ie%3DUTF-8%26oe%3DUTF-8%26selm%3D5f25b5cf.0301230204.71170b4c%2540posting.google.com

I had to write an undefinite number of tapes, every tape containing
one file with same structure. You have to read the same thing.
The clue is dynamic allocation of tapes through an Assembler
subroutine.
In my program, after the first tape is allocated to program, file it's
written, file closed and tape deallocated. Now the second tape can be
mounted, allocated to program and so on.
I don't know if dynamic allocation is allowed under VSE, this can be
really sad.
Another push to upgrade. ;)
Regards,
Mircea
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: use of CLOSE UNIT FOR REMOVAL

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-08T10:47:07-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c2ibiu$1ta2o2$1@ID-184804.news.uni-berlin.de>`
- **References:** `<c27sds$1q6m0m$1@ID-184804.news.uni-berlin.de> <5f25b5cf.0403070727.77973034@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi Mircea,

Actually, following your link I was able to find other link which gave the
the answer I was looking for.  That link is:
http://groups.google.com/groups?hl=en&lr=&ie=UTF-8&newwindow=1&threadm=B0000
107577%40apps.escape.net.au&rnum=1&prev=/groups%3Fhl%3Den%26lr%3D%26ie%3DUTF
-8%26newwindow%3D1%26selm%3DB0000107577%2540apps.escape.net.au

This link may only apply to VSE, but anyway the answer is very simple.  So
simple it's embarassing, actually!  Basically, it's just the following:
CLOSE filename REEL FOR REMOVAL
CLOSE filename
OPEN INPUT filename

What I had been trying to do was eject the tape and process the next tape as
part of the "same file", kind of as if it was a single file spanning more
than one tape.  The above way simply treats the new tape as, well, a new
tape.  Which is the way the program was working in the first place, with the
only difference being the old way was something like:
CLOSE filename
STOP "OPERATOR: Please eject current tape and enter new tape, then press
Enter"
OPEN INPUT filename

Thanks for the pointer!  I had done a google groups search but had not seen
what I was looking for.

--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA
```

#### ↳ Re: Sending Mail From Cobol

- **From:** superk <member@mainframeforum.com>

```
Chances are that your file is a LINE SEQUENTIAL not (default - ANSI conforming)
RECORD Sequential.  Make the following changes and see how it goes:

   SELECT MICLIENT
                ASSIGN TO "H:\ACCOUNTS.CSV"
                     ORGANIZATION IS  line SEQUENTIAL
       *              PADDING CHARACTER IS ","
       *              RECORD DELIMITER STANDARD-1
                     FILE STATUS IS CU-STAT.
    ...

       FD  MICLIENT
       *      BLOCK CONTAINS 2 RECORDS
       *      RECORD CONTAINS 10 TO 109 CHARACTERS
       *     LABEL RECORD IS STANDARD
                            .
```

```
My guess is that you didn't catch all of Bill's changes.  In addition
to changing to line sequential, the variable length record
specification was removed form the FD.

Contrary to other messages "39" is not a file not found, that would
have given you a "35".  "39" is a fixed file attribute problem - which
I expect to see if you use Line Sequential WITH the variable length
record specification.

"frank" <applied_software@msn.com> wrote in message news:<c292p5$lak$1@zook.lafn.org>...
> Hi there,
> If I change to line sequential, it togles the file status to 48 from 39; and
…[91 more quoted lines elided]…
> >
```

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** Donald Tees <donald_tees@nospam.sympatico.ca>

- **Message-ID:** `<DI42c.9352$jw2.647785@news20.bellglobal.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<bfdfc3e8.0403050921.3367b0e1@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<c283cb$ak9$1@zook.lafn.org> <h36f40lsrjul7c60pljf13so50g9j9pkp8@4ax.com> <c286co$bkv$1@zook.lafn.org> <RkN1c.19225$yZ1.18131@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <c292p5$lak$1@zook.lafn.org> <bfdfc3e8.0403050921.3367b0e1@posting.google.com>`

```
Thane Hubbell wrote:
> My guess is that you didn't catch all of Bill's changes.  In addition
> to changing to line sequential, the variable length record
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> 
This is what I use for fujitsu cobol CSV files. I think you will get a 
39 error if you try to read a line over 1000 characters long, but 
otherwise you should get the line length back in sequential-record-size 
up until an "AT END" statement. The data persists after both errors and 
closes if you want to code up a DECLARATIONS section.  That's 
non-standard, but it is there.

Donald

            SELECT SEQUENTIAL-FILE ASSIGN TO SEQUENTIAL-ID
                ACCESS MODE IS SEQUENTIAL
                FILE STATUS IS SEQUENTIAL-STATUS
                ORGANIZATION IS LINE SEQUENTIAL.
        DATA DIVISION.
        FILE SECTION.
        FD SEQUENTIAL-FILE
            RECORD IS VARYING IN SIZE
            FROM 1 TO 1000 CHARACTERS
            DEPENDING ON SEQUENTIAL-RECORD-SIZE.
        01 SEQUENTIAL-RECORD                 PICTURE X(1000).
        WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
        77 sequential-record-size            picture 9(4).
        77 SEQUENTIAL-STATUS                 picture xx.
        77 SEQUENTIAL-ID                     PICTURE X(80).
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: reading a csv file generated with access

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-03-04T21:05:34-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0403042105.50d86efd@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<c283cb$ak9$1@zook.lafn.org> <h36f40lsrjul7c60pljf13so50g9j9pkp8@4ax.com> <c286co$bkv$1@zook.lafn.org>`

```
"frank" <applied_software@msn.com> wrote

> The compiler is fujitsu v3.
> and the way is presented below is sending a 39 status at opening, it does
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>                ASSIGN TO "H:\ACCOUNTS.CSV"

File staus '39' is file not found.  There is no file called
'H:\ACCOUNTS.CSV' so the OPEN INPUT failed.

If you had ignored this and gone on to do something else with the file
then you would get strange file status codes because the file is not
open.

The implication of the '.CSV' on the file name is that it is a Comma
Separated Value file.  This cannot be read into a record area directly
as the fields are not in fixed positions.  If it is a CSV then you
will need to declare it LINE SEQUENTIAL and separate the fields
yourself.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: reading a csv file generated with access

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2004-03-05T06:42:19-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Q8OdnUj33JEG6NXdRVn-hw@giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<c283cb$ak9$1@zook.lafn.org> <h36f40lsrjul7c60pljf13so50g9j9pkp8@4ax.com> <c286co$bkv$1@zook.lafn.org> <217e491a.0403042105.50d86efd@posting.google.com>`

```
Richard wrote:
> "frank" <applied_software@msn.com> wrote
>
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> 'H:\ACCOUNTS.CSV' so the OPEN INPUT failed.

No, "39" is "Conflict between fixed and defined file attributes."

This means that the actual file on the disk does not conform to the
program's file definition.

"35" is file not found.
```
